<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Colorado</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the U.S. state of Colorado. For the river, see <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>. For the physiographic region, see <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Colorado_(disambiguation)" title="Colorado (disambiguation)">Colorado (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Colorado</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:ColoradanColorado.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7f/ColoradanColorado.ogg" title="ColoradanColorado.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>) is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> encompassing most of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a> as well as the northeastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a> and the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. Colorado is part of the <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">Western United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a>. Colorado is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">8th-most extensive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">21st-most populous</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50_United_States" title="50 United States">50 United States</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Colorado was 5,540,545 on July 1, 2016, an increase of 10.17% since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state was named for the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Conquistador#North_America_exploration" title="Conquistador">Spanish travelers</a> named the <i>Río Colorado</i> for the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ruddy" title="wiktionary:ruddy">ruddy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/colorado" title="wiktionary:colorado">colorado</a></i></span>) <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">silt</a> the river carried from the mountains. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a> was organized on February 28, 1861, and on August 1, 1876, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> signed Proclamation 230 admitting Colorado to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the 38th state. Colorado is nicknamed the "<a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_nicknames" title="List of U.S. state nicknames">Centennial State</a>" because it became a state a century after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>.</p>
<p>Colorado is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> to the southwest at the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a>. Colorado is noted for its vivid landscape of mountains, forests, <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">high plains</a>, mesas, canyons, <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a>, rivers, and desert lands.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> is the capital and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities_by_population" title="Colorado municipalities by population">most populous city</a> of Colorado. Residents of the state are properly known as <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Colorado" title="List of people from Colorado">Coloradans</a>, although the term "Coloradoan" has been used archaically and lives on in the title of Fort Collins' newspaper, the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins_Coloradoan" title="Fort Collins Coloradoan">Coloradoan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statestyle_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-statestyle-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coloradan_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coloradan-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Colorado" title="Geography of Colorado">Geography of Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado is notable for its diverse geography, ranging from alpine mountains, arid plains and deserts with huge sand dunes, deep canyons, sandstone and granite rock formations, rivers, lakes, and lush forests. The borders of Colorado were originally defined to be lines of latitude and longitude, making its shape a latitude-longitude quadrangle which stretches from <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a> to <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°N</a> latitude and from <a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="25th meridian west from Washington">102°03'W</a> to <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">109°03'W</a> longitude (<a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="25th meridian west from Washington">25°W</a> to <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">32°W</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Meridian" title="Washington Meridian">Washington Meridian</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colorado_Enabling_Act_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_Enabling_Act-13">[13]</a></sup> Colorado, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> are the only states which have boundaries defined solely by lines of latitude and longitude.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elkmts.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2021" data-file-width="3072" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Elkmts.JPG/220px-Elkmts.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Elkmts.JPG/330px-Elkmts.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Elkmts.JPG/440px-Elkmts.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains">Mountains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Mountains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_peaks_of_Colorado" title="Mountain peaks of Colorado">Mountain peaks of Colorado</a></div>
<p>The summit of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbert" title="Mount Elbert">Mount Elbert</a> at 14,440 feet (4,401.2 m) elevation in <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_Colorado" title="Lake County, Colorado">Lake County</a> is the highest point in Colorado and the Rocky Mountains of North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mount_Elbert_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mount_Elbert-4">[4]</a></sup> Colorado is the only U.S. state that lies entirely above 1,000 meters' elevation. The point where the <a href="/wiki/Arikaree_River" title="Arikaree River">Arikaree River</a> flows out of <a href="/wiki/Yuma_County,_Colorado" title="Yuma County, Colorado">Yuma County, Colorado</a>, and into <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_County,_Kansas" title="Cheyenne County, Kansas">Cheyenne County, Kansas</a>, is the lowest point in Colorado at 3,317 feet (1,011 m) elevation. This point, which holds the distinction of being the highest low elevation point of any state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> is higher than the high elevation points of 18 states and the District of Columbia.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Picketwire_Canyon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/220px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/330px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/440px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Picketwire_Canyon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of the arid high plains in Southeastern Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calhanpm.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Calhanpm.JPG/220px-Calhanpm.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Calhanpm.JPG/330px-Calhanpm.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Calhanpm.JPG/440px-Calhanpm.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Calhanpm.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calhan_Paint_Mines" title="Calhan Paint Mines">Calhan Paint Mines</a> on the Colorado Eastern Plains</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plains">Plains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Plains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A little less than one half of the area of Colorado is flat and rolling land. East of the Rocky Mountains are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_Eastern_Plains" title="Colorado Eastern Plains">Colorado Eastern Plains</a> of the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a>, the section of the Great Plains within Nebraska at elevations ranging from roughly 3,350 to 7,500 feet (1,020 to 2,290 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The Colorado plains were mostly prairies, but they have many patches of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deciduous_forests" title="Deciduous forests">deciduous forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butte" title="Butte">buttes</a>, and canyons. Eastern Colorado is presently mainly covered in farmland and rangeland, along with small farming villages and towns. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is fair, averaging from 15 to 25 inches (380 to 640 mm) annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccc_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-16">[16]</a></sup> Corn, wheat, hay, soybeans, and oats are all typical crops, and most of the villages and towns in this region boast both a water tower and a <a href="/wiki/Grain_elevator" title="Grain elevator">grain elevator</a>. Irrigation water is available from the South Platte, the Arkansas River, and a few other streams, and also from subterranean sources, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artesian_well" title="Artesian well">artesian wells</a>. However, heavy use of ground water from wells for irrigation has caused underground water reserves to decline. As well as crop agriculture, eastern Colorado hosts considerable livestock, such as cattle ranches and hog farms.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Front_range">Front range</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Front range">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Condiv.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2746" data-file-width="4320" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/220px-Condiv.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/330px-Condiv.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/440px-Condiv.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Condiv.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a> Peaks west of Denver</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roughly 70% of Colorado's population resides along the eastern edge of the Rocky Mountains in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a> between <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne,_Wyoming" title="Cheyenne, Wyoming">Cheyenne, Wyoming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo, Colorado</a>. This region is partially protected from prevailing storms that blow in from the Pacific Ocean region by the high Rockies in the middle of Colorado. The "Front Range" includes Denver, Boulder, Fort Collins, Loveland, Colorado Springs, Pueblo, Greeley and other townships and municipalities in between. On the other side of the Rockies, the significant population centers in Western Colorado (which is not considered the "Front Range") are the cities of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">Grand Junction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Colorado" title="Durango, Colorado">Durango</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Colorado" title="Montrose, Colorado">Montrose</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continental_Divide">Continental Divide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Continental Divide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG/220px-Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG/330px-Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG/440px-Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Continental-Divide_Monarch-Pass_2012-10-28.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_of_the_Americas" title="Continental Divide of the Americas">Continental Divide</a> at <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Pass" title="Monarch Pass">Monarch Pass</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_of_the_Americas" title="Continental Divide of the Americas">Continental Divide of the Americas</a> extends along the crest of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The area of Colorado to the west of the Continental Divide is called the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Western_Slope" title="Colorado Western Slope">Western Slope of Colorado</a>. Drainage water west of the Continental Divide flows to the southwest via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_River_(U.S.)" title="Colorado River (U.S.)">Colorado River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.</p>
<p>Within the interior of the Rocky Mountains are several large parks which are high broad basins. In the north, on the east side of the Continental Divide is the <a href="/wiki/North_Park_(Colorado_basin)" title="North Park (Colorado basin)">North Park of Colorado</a>. The North Park is drained by the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte River</a>, which flows north into Wyoming and Nebraska. Just to the south of North Park, but on the western side of the Continental Divide, is the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Park_(Colorado_basin)" title="Middle Park (Colorado basin)">Middle Park of Colorado</a>, which is drained by the Colorado River. The <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(Park_County,_Colorado)" title="South Park (Park County, Colorado)">South Park of Colorado</a> is the region of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Headwater" title="Headwater">headwaters</a> of the South Platte River.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_region">Southern region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Southern region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mt_Herard_sand.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mt_Herard_sand.JPG/220px-Mt_Herard_sand.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mt_Herard_sand.JPG/330px-Mt_Herard_sand.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mt_Herard_sand.JPG/440px-Mt_Herard_sand.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mt_Herard_sand.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The tallest dunes in North America at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Sand_Dunes_National_Park" title="Great Sand Dunes National Park">Great Sand Dunes National Park</a> in southern Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In southmost Colorado is the large <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Valley" title="San Luis Valley">San Luis Valley</a>, where the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> are located. The valley sits between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangre_De_Cristo_Mountains" title="Sangre De Cristo Mountains">Sangre De Cristo Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a>, and consists of large desert lands that eventually run into the mountains. The Rio Grande drains due south into New Mexico, Mexico, and Texas. Across the <a href="/wiki/Sangre_de_Cristo_Range" title="Sangre de Cristo Range">Sangre de Cristo Range</a> to the east of the San Luis Valley lies the <a href="/wiki/Wet_Mountain_Valley" title="Wet Mountain Valley">Wet Mountain Valley</a>. These basins, particularly the San Luis Valley, lie along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_Rift" title="Rio Grande Rift">Rio Grande Rift</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Geological_formation" title="Geological formation">geological formation</a> of the Rocky Mountains, and its branches.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChicoClosedBasin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="832" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/220px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/330px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/440px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChicoClosedBasin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The high desert lands that make up the San Luis Valley in Southern Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peaks">Peaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Peaks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_peaks_of_Colorado" title="Mountain peaks of Colorado">Mountain peaks of Colorado</a></div>
<p>To the west of the Great Plains of Colorado rises the eastern slope of the Rocky Mountains. Notable peaks of the Rocky Mountains include <a href="/wiki/Longs_Peak" title="Longs Peak">Longs Peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Evans" title="Mount Evans">Mount Evans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak" title="Pikes Peak">Pikes Peak</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Peaks" title="Spanish Peaks">Spanish Peaks</a> near <a href="/wiki/Walsenburg,_Colorado" title="Walsenburg, Colorado">Walsenburg</a>, in southern Colorado. This area drains to the east and the southeast, ultimately either via the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SANJUANMTNS.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2846" data-file-width="4320" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/SANJUANMTNS.JPG/220px-SANJUANMTNS.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/SANJUANMTNS.JPG/330px-SANJUANMTNS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/SANJUANMTNS.JPG/440px-SANJUANMTNS.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SANJUANMTNS.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Peaks of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Rocky Mountains within Colorado contain about 53 peaks that are 14,000 feet (4,267 m) or higher in elevation above sea level, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_fourteeners" title="Colorado fourteeners">fourteeners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> These mountains are largely covered with trees such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">conifers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aspen" title="Aspen">aspens</a> up to the <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a>, at an elevation of about 12,000 feet (3,700 m) in southern Colorado to about 10,500 feet (3,200 m) in northern Colorado. Above this only alpine vegetation grows. Only small parts of the Colorado Rockies are snow-covered year round.</p>
<p>Much of the alpine snow melts by mid-August with the exception of a few snowcapped peaks and a few small glaciers. The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mineral_Belt" title="Colorado Mineral Belt">Colorado Mineral Belt</a>, stretching from the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a> in the southwest to <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_City,_Colorado" title="Central City, Colorado">Central City</a> on the front range, contains most of the historic gold- and silver-mining districts of Colorado. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbert" title="Mount Elbert">Mount Elbert</a> is the highest summit of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The 30 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest_mountain_peaks_of_the_Rocky_Mountains" title="Highest mountain peaks of the Rocky Mountains">highest major summits</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> of North America all lie within the state.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackCanyon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/BlackCanyon.JPG/220px-BlackCanyon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/BlackCanyon.JPG/330px-BlackCanyon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/BlackCanyon.JPG/440px-BlackCanyon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlackCanyon.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Black_Canyon_of_the_Gunnison_National_Park" title="Black Canyon of the Gunnison National Park">Black Canyon of the Gunnison National Park</a> near <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Colorado" title="Montrose, Colorado">Montrose</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East_rim_arch.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1494" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/East_rim_arch.jpg/220px-East_rim_arch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/East_rim_arch.jpg/330px-East_rim_arch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/East_rim_arch.jpg/440px-East_rim_arch.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Rim Arch in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Ridge_Canyons_Wilderness" title="Black Ridge Canyons Wilderness">Black Ridge Canyons Wilderness</a> in western Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Redcanyon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Redcanyon.JPG/220px-Redcanyon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Redcanyon.JPG/330px-Redcanyon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Redcanyon.JPG/440px-Redcanyon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colorado_Western_Slope">Colorado Western Slope</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Colorado Western Slope">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Valley,_Colorado.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1742" data-file-width="2322" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg/220px-Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg/330px-Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg/440px-Grand_Valley%2C_Colorado.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Valley,_Colorado.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Grand Valley in Western Colorado, a large valley made up of high desert terrain. The city of Grand Junction is located in the heart of the valley</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Western Slope of Colorado is drained by the Colorado River and its tributaries (primarily the <a href="/wiki/Gunnison_River" title="Gunnison River">Gunnison River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_River_(Colorado_River)" title="San Juan River (Colorado River)">San Juan River</a>) or by evaporation in its arid areas. The Colorado River flows through <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Canyon" title="Glenwood Canyon">Glenwood Canyon</a> and then through an arid valley made up of desert from <a href="/wiki/Rifle,_Colorado" title="Rifle, Colorado">Rifle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Parachute,_Colorado" title="Parachute, Colorado">Parachute</a>, through the desert canyon of <a href="/wiki/De_Beque_Canyon" title="De Beque Canyon">De Beque Canyon</a>, and into the arid desert of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Valley_(Colorado-Utah)" title="Grand Valley (Colorado-Utah)">Grand Valley</a>, where the city of Grand Junction is located. Also prominent in or near the southern portion of the Western Slope are the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Mesa" title="Grand Mesa">Grand Mesa</a>, which lies to the southeast of Grand Junction; the high San Juan Mountains, a rugged mountain range; and to the west of the San Juan Mountains, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a>, a high arid region that borders Southern Utah.</p>
<p>The city of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">Grand Junction, Colorado</a> is the largest city on the Western Slope. Grand Junction and Durango are the only major centers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_broadcasting" title="Television broadcasting">television broadcasting</a> west of the Continental Divide in Colorado, though most mountain resort communities publish daily newspapers. Higher education in and near the Western Slope can be found at <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mesa_University" title="Colorado Mesa University">Colorado Mesa University</a> in Grand Junction, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_State_College_of_Colorado" title="Western State College of Colorado">Western State College of Colorado</a> in Gunnison, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lewis_College" title="Fort Lewis College">Fort Lewis College</a> in Durango, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mountain_College" title="Colorado Mountain College">Colorado Mountain College</a> in Glenwood Springs and Steamboat Springs.</p>
<p>Grand Junction is located along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 70 in Colorado">Interstate 70</a>, the only major highway in Western Colorado. Grand Junction is also along the major railroad of the Western Slope, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Pacific" title="Union Pacific">Union Pacific</a>. This railroad also provides the tracks for <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>'s <a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyr</a> passenger train, which crosses the Rocky Mountains between Denver and Grand Junction via a route on which there are no continuous highways.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colorado_National_Monument_(4939640266).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/220px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/330px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/440px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colorado_National_Monument_(4939640266).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Colorado National Monument near Grand Junction. The monument is made up of high desert canyons and sandstone rock formations</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Western Slope lies in close proximity to multiple notable destinations in the Colorado Rocky Mountains, including <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Springs,_Colorado" title="Glenwood Springs, Colorado">Glenwood Springs</a>, with its resort hot springs, and the <a href="/wiki/Ski_resort" title="Ski resort">ski resorts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breckenridge,_Colorado" title="Breckenridge, Colorado">Breckenridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vail,_Colorado" title="Vail, Colorado">Vail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crested_Butte,_Colorado" title="Crested Butte, Colorado">Crested Butte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steamboat_Springs,_Colorado" title="Steamboat Springs, Colorado">Steamboat Springs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telluride,_Colorado" title="Telluride, Colorado">Telluride</a>.</p>
<p>The northwestern corner of Colorado is a sparsely populated region, and it contains part of the noted <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur_National_Monument" title="Dinosaur National Monument">Dinosaur National Monument</a>, which is not only a <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontological</a> area, but is also a scenic area of rocky hills, canyons, arid desert, and streambeds. Here, the Green River briefly crosses over into Colorado.</p>
<p>From west to east, the land of Colorado consists of desert lands, desert plateaus, alpine mountains, National Forests, relatively flat grasslands, scattered forests, buttes, and canyons in the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. The famous <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak" title="Pikes Peak">Pikes Peak</a> is located just west of <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a>. Its isolated peak is visible from nearly the Kansas border on clear days, and also far to the north and the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Desert lands in Colorado are located in and around areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canon_City,_Colorado" title="Canon City, Colorado">Canon City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence,_Colorado" title="Florence, Colorado">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Sand_Dunes_National_Park_and_Preserve" title="Great Sand Dunes National Park and Preserve">Great Sand Dunes National Park and Preserve</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Valley" title="San Luis Valley">San Luis Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cortez,_Colorado" title="Cortez, Colorado">Cortez</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canyon_of_the_Ancients_National_Monument" title="Canyon of the Ancients National Monument">Canyon of the Ancients National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hovenweep_National_Monument" title="Hovenweep National Monument">Hovenweep National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ute_Mountain" title="Ute Mountain">Ute Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta,_Colorado" title="Delta, Colorado">Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">Grand Junction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_National_Monument" title="Colorado National Monument">Colorado National Monument</a>, and other areas surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Uncompahgre_Plateau" title="Uncompahgre Plateau">Uncompahgre Plateau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uncompahgre_National_Forest" title="Uncompahgre National Forest">Uncompahgre National Forest</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Four_Corners_Monument_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg/220px-Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg/330px-Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg/440px-Four_Corners_Monument_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Four_Corners_Monument_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Ute_Mountain" title="Ute Mountain">Ute Mountain</a> in the distance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Colorado is one of four states in the United States that share a common geographic point – the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a> together with Arizona, New Mexico, and Utah. At this intersection, it is possible to stand in four states at once.</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_cities_and_towns" title="Colorado cities and towns">Colorado cities and towns</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Colorado" title="List of counties in Colorado">List of counties in Colorado</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities" title="Colorado municipalities">Colorado municipalities</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_rivers" title="Colorado rivers">Colorado rivers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CO_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1305" data-file-width="1260" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CO_koppen.svg/300px-CO_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CO_koppen.svg/450px-CO_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CO_koppen.svg/600px-CO_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CO_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> of Colorado is more complex than states outside of the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a> region. Unlike most other states, southern Colorado is not always warmer than northern Colorado. Most of Colorado is made up of mountains, foothills, high plains, and desert lands. Mountains and surrounding valleys greatly affect local climate.</p>
<p>As a general rule, with an increase in elevation comes a decrease in temperature and an increase in precipitation. Northeast, east, and southeast Colorado are mostly the high plains, while Northern Colorado is a mix of high plains, foothills, and mountains. Northwest and west Colorado are predominantly mountainous, with some desert lands mixed in. Southwest and southern Colorado are a complex mixture of desert and mountain areas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Plains">Eastern Plains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Eastern Plains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of the Eastern Plains is <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semiarid</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Cold semi-arid climate"><i>BSk</i></a>) with low humidity and moderate precipitation, usually from 15 to 25 inches (380 to 640 millimetres) annually. The area is known for its abundant sunshine and cool, clear nights, which give this area a great average <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature range</a>. The difference between the highs of the days and the lows of the nights can be considerable as warmth dissipates to space during clear nights, the heat radiation not being trapped by clouds.</p>
<p>The Front Range urban corridor, where most of the population of Colorado resides, lies in a pronounced <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">precipitation shadow</a> as a result of being on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeward" title="Leeward">lee</a> side of the Rocky Mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgsFRUC1978_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgsFRUC1978-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In summer, this area can have many days above 95 °F (35 °C) and often 100 °F (38 °C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_of_Colorado_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_of_Colorado-20">[20]</a></sup> On the plains, the winter lows usually range from 25 to −10 °F (−4 to −23 °C). About 75% of the precipitation falls within the growing season, from April to September, but this area is very prone to droughts. Most of the precipitation comes from thunderstorms, which can be severe, and from major snowstorms that occur in the winter and early spring. Otherwise, winters tend to be mostly dry and cold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In much of the region, March is the snowiest month. April and May are normally the rainiest months, while April is the wettest month overall. The Front Range cities closer to the mountains tend to be warmer in the winter due to <a href="/wiki/Chinook_wind" title="Chinook wind">Chinook winds</a> which warm the area, sometimes bringing temperatures of 70 °F (21 °C) or higher in the winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America-21">[21]</a></sup> The average July temperature is 55 °F (13 °C) in the morning and 90 °F (32 °C) in the afternoon. The average January temperature is 18 °F (−8 °C) in the morning and 48 °F (9 °C) in the afternoon, although variation between consecutive days can be 40 °F (20 °C).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Front_range_foothills">Front range foothills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Front range foothills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Just west of the plains and into the foothills, there are a wide variety of climate types. Locations merely a few miles apart can experience entirely different weather depending on the topography. Most valleys have a semi-arid climate not unlike the eastern plains, which transitions to an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine climate</a> at the highest elevations. Microclimates also exist in local areas that run nearly the entire spectrum of climates, including subtropical highland (<i>Cfb/Cwb</i>), humid subtropical (<i>Cfa</i>), humid continental (<i>Dfa/Dfb</i>), Mediterranean (<i>Csa/Csb</i>) and subarctic (<i>Dfc</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_weather">Extreme weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Extreme weather">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4400" data-file-width="5600" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg/220px-October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg/330px-October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg/440px-October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:October_Snow_in_Colorado.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Snow highlights the rugged mountains, as well as the urban and agricultural landscapes of the Colorado plains.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Extreme weather changes are common in Colorado, although the majority of extreme weather occurs in the least populated areas of the state. Thunderstorms are common east of the Continental Divide in the spring and summer, yet are usually brief. Hail is a common sight in the mountains east of the divide and in the northwest part of the state. The Eastern Plains have had some of the biggest hail storms in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccc_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Eastern Plains are part of the extreme western portion of <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>; some damaging tornadoes in the Eastern Plains include the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Limon,_Colorado" title="Limon, Colorado">Limon</a> <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">F3</a> tornado and the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Colorado" title="Windsor, Colorado">Windsor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enhanced_Fujita_Scale" title="Enhanced Fujita Scale">EF3</a> tornado, which devastated the small town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The plains are also susceptible to occasional floods, which are caused both by thunderstorms and by the rapid melting of snow in the mountains during warm weather. Notable examples include the <a href="/wiki/Big_Thompson_River" title="Big Thompson River">Big Thompson River</a> flooding of 1976 and the <a href="/wiki/2013_Colorado_floods" title="2013 Colorado floods">2013 Colorado floods</a>. Denver's record in 1901 for the number of consecutive days above 90 °F (32 °C) was broken during the summer of 2008. The new record of 24 consecutive days surpassed the previous record by almost a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Much of Colorado is a very dry state averaging only 17 inches (430 millimetres) of precipitation per year statewide and rarely experiences a time when some portion of the state is not in some degree of drought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The lack of precipitation contributes to the severity of wildfires in the state, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hayman_Fire" title="Hayman Fire">Hayman Fire</a>, one of the largest wildfires in American history, and the <a href="/wiki/Fourmile_Canyon#Fourmile_Canyon_Fire" title="Fourmile Canyon">Fourmile Canyon Fire</a> of 2010, which until the <a href="/wiki/Waldo_Canyon_Fire" title="Waldo Canyon Fire">Waldo Canyon Fire</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Park_Fire" title="High Park Fire">High Park Fire</a> of June 2012, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest_Fire" title="Black Forest Fire">Black Forest Fire</a> of June 2013, was the most destructive wildfire in Colorado's recorded history.</p>
<p>However, some of the mountainous regions of Colorado receive a huge amount of moisture from winter snowfalls. The spring melts of these snows often cause great waterflows in the <a href="/wiki/Yampa_River" title="Yampa River">Yampa River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, the Rio Grande, the Arkansas River, the North Platte River, and the South Platte River.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg/250px-Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg/375px-Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg/500px-Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Overlook_of_Yampa_River.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Yampa River, from a high overlook</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Water flowing out of the Colorado Rocky Mountains is a very significant source of water for the farms, towns, and cities of the southwest states of New Mexico, Arizona, Utah, and Nevada, as well as the Midwest, such as Nebraska and Kansas, and the southern states of Oklahoma and Texas. A significant amount of water is also diverted for use in California; occasionally (formerly naturally and consistently), the flow of water reaches northern Mexico.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The highest ambient air temperature ever recorded in Colorado was 118 °F (48 °C) on July 11, 1888, at <a href="/wiki/Bennett,_Colorado" title="Bennett, Colorado">Bennett</a>. The lowest air temperature was −61 °F (−52 °C) on February 1, 1985, at <a href="/wiki/Maybell,_Colorado" title="Maybell, Colorado">Maybell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateMaxTemps_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-StateMaxTemps-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateMinTemps_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-StateMinTemps-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tr>
