<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite its mountainous terrain, Colorado is relatively quiet seismically. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Earthquake_Information_Center" title="National Earthquake Information Center">National Earthquake Information Center</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Golden,_Colorado" title="Golden, Colorado">Golden</a>.</p>
<p>On August 22, 2011, a <a href="/wiki/2011_Colorado_earthquake" title="2011 Colorado earthquake">5.3 magnitude earthquake</a> occurred 9 miles (14 km) west-southwest of the city of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Colorado" title="Trinidad, Colorado">Trinidad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> There were no casualties and only a small amount of damage was reported. It was the second largest earthquake in Colorado. A magnitude 5.7 earthquake was recorded in 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1543" data-file-width="2126" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/220px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/330px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/440px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Palace" title="Cliff Palace">Cliff Palace</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde National Park</a> as photographed by <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Nordenski%C3%B6ld" title="Gustaf Nordenskiöld">Gustaf Nordenskiöld</a> in 1891.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG/220px-Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG/330px-Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG/440px-Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Kiva_at_Chimney_Rock_Colorado.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Great Kiva at Chimney Rock in the San Juan Mountains of Southwestern Colorado. It is said to have been built by the Ancient Pueblo peoples.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Colorado" title="History of Colorado">History of Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Colorado_history" title="Timeline of Colorado history">Timeline of Colorado history</a></div>
<p>The region that is today the state of Colorado has been inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> for more than 13,000 years. The <a href="/wiki/Lindenmeier_Site" title="Lindenmeier Site">Lindenmeier Site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Larimer_County,_Colorado" title="Larimer County, Colorado">Larimer County</a> contains <a href="/wiki/Artifact_(archaeology)" title="Artifact (archaeology)">artifacts</a> dating from approximately 11200 BC to 3000 BC. The eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">major migration route</a> that was important to the spread of early peoples throughout the Americas. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Pueblo_peoples" title="Ancient Pueblo peoples">Ancient Pueblo peoples</a> lived in the valleys and mesas of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ute_Nation" title="Ute Nation">Ute Nation</a> inhabited the mountain valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Rocky_Mountains" title="Western Rocky Mountains">Western Rocky Mountains</a>, even as far east as the Front Range of present day. The <a href="/wiki/Apache" title="Apache">Apache</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">Comanche</a> also inhabited Eastern and Southeastern parts of the state. At times, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arapaho_Nation" title="Arapaho Nation">Arapaho Nation</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Nation" title="Cheyenne Nation">Cheyenne Nation</a> moved west to hunt across the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a>.</p>
<p>The U.S. acquired a territorial claim to the eastern Rocky Mountains with the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> from France in 1803. This U.S. claim conflicted with the claim by Spain to the upper <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas River Basin</a> as the exclusive trading zone of its colony of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_F%C3%A9_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fé de Nuevo México">Santa Fé de Nuevo México</a>. In 1806, <a href="/wiki/Zebulon_Pike" title="Zebulon Pike">Zebulon Pike</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Pike_expedition" title="Pike expedition">U.S. Army reconnaissance expedition</a> into the disputed region. Colonel Pike and his men were arrested by Spanish cavalrymen in the <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Valley" title="San Luis Valley">San Luis Valley</a> the following February, taken to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chihuahua,_Chihuahua" title="Chihuahua, Chihuahua">Chihuahua</a>, and expelled from Mexico the following July.</p>
<p>The U.S. relinquished its claim to all land south and west of the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas River</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42nd parallel north</a> and west of the <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_west" title="100th meridian west">100th meridian west</a> as part of its purchase of Florida from Spain with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adams-On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams-Onís Treaty">Adams-Onís Treaty</a> of 1819. The treaty took effect February 22, 1821. Having settled its border with Spain, the U.S. admitted the southeastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Territory" title="Missouri Territory">Territory of Missouri</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">state of Missouri</a> on August 10, 1821. The remainder of Missouri Territory, including what would become northeastern Colorado, became unorganized territory, and remained so for 33 years over the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">question of slavery</a>. After 11 years of war, Spain finally recognized the independence of Mexico with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Treaty of Córdoba">Treaty of Córdoba</a> signed on August 24, 1821. Mexico eventually ratified the Adams-Onís Treaty in 1831. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texian_Revolt" title="Texian Revolt">Texian Revolt</a> of 1835–36 fomented a dispute between the U.S. and Mexico which eventually erupted into the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> in 1846. Mexico surrendered its northern territory to the U.S. with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a> at the conclusion of the war in 1848.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="941" data-file-width="1068" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/220px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/330px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/440px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Mexican cession, with the white representing the territory the United States received from Mexico. Well over half of Colorado was received during this treaty.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most American <a href="/wiki/Settler" title="Settler">settlers</a> traveling overland west to the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">Oregon Country</a>, namely the new goldfields of California, or the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">Mormon</a> settlements of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Valley" title="Salt Lake Valley">Salt Lake Valley</a>, avoided the rugged <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a>, and instead followed the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweetwater_River_(Wyoming)" title="Sweetwater River (Wyoming)">Sweetwater River</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_Pass_(Wyoming)" title="South Pass (Wyoming)">South Pass (Wyoming)</a>, the lowest crossing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_Divide" title="Continental Divide">Continental Divide</a> between the Southern Rocky Mountains and the Central Rocky Mountains. In 1849, the Mormons of the Salt Lake Valley organized the extralegal <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a>, claiming the entire <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a> and all lands drained by the rivers <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Grand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado</a>. The federal government of the U.S. flatly refused to recognize the new Mormon government, because it was <a href="/wiki/History_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints#Brigham_Young.27s_early_theocratic_leadership" title="History of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">theocratic</a> and sanctioned <a href="/wiki/Mormonism_and_polygamy" title="Mormonism and polygamy">plural marriage</a>. Instead, the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1850" title="Compromise of 1850">Compromise of 1850</a> divided the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">Mexican Cession</a> and the northwestern claims of Texas into a new state and two new territories, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_California" title="State of California">state of California</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Mexico" title="Territory of New Mexico">Territory of New Mexico</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Utah" title="Territory of Utah">Territory of Utah</a>. On April 9, 1851, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexican American</a> settlers from the area of <a href="/wiki/Taos,_New_Mexico" title="Taos, New Mexico">Taos</a> settled the village of <a href="/wiki/San_Luis,_Colorado" title="San Luis, Colorado">San Luis</a>, then in the <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">New Mexico Territory</a>, later to become Colorado's first permanent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_American" title="European American">Euro-American</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Settlement_(migration)" title="Settlement (migration)">settlement</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="1024" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg/220px-Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg/330px-Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg/440px-Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anasazi_Heritage_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Anasazi Heritage Center in <a href="/wiki/Dolores,_Colorado" title="Dolores, Colorado">Dolores</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1854, Senator <a href="/wiki/Stephen_A._Douglas" title="Stephen A. Douglas">Stephen A. Douglas</a> persuaded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">U.S. Congress</a> to divide the unorganized territory east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_Divide" title="Continental Divide">Continental Divide</a> into two new organized territories, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Kansas" title="Territory of Kansas">Territory of Kansas</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Nebraska" title="Territory of Nebraska">Territory of Nebraska</a>, and an unorganized southern region known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_territory" title="Indian territory">Indian territory</a>. Each new territory was to decide the fate of slavery within its boundaries, but this compromise merely served to fuel animosity between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_soil" title="Free soil">free soil</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proslavery_in_the_antebellum_United_States" title="Proslavery in the antebellum United States">pro-slavery</a> factions.</p>
<p>The gold seekers organized the <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Territory" title="Jefferson Territory">Provisional Government of the Territory of Jefferson</a> on August 24, 1859, but this new territory failed to secure approval from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" title="Congress of the United States">Congress of the United States</a> embroiled in the debate over slavery. The election of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> for the President of the United States on November 6, 1860, led to the <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> of nine southern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_states" title="Slave states">slave states</a> and the threat of <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">civil war among the states</a>. Seeking to augment the political power of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_state_(United_States)" title="Free state (United States)">Union states</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>-dominated Congress quickly admitted the eastern portion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Kansas" title="Territory of Kansas">Territory of Kansas</a> into the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the free <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">State of Kansas</a> on January 29, 1861, leaving the western portion of the Kansas Territory, and its gold-mining areas, as unorganized territory.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territory_act">Territory act</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Territory act">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1860_colorado_territory_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="448" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1860_colorado_territory_map.png/220px-1860_colorado_territory_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1860_colorado_territory_map.png/330px-1860_colorado_territory_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1860_colorado_territory_map.png/440px-1860_colorado_territory_map.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1860_colorado_territory_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The territories of <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Territory" title="Utah Territory">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Territory" title="Nebraska Territory">Nebraska</a> before the creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thirty days later on February 28, 1861, outgoing U.S. President <a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">James Buchanan</a> signed an Act of Congress organizing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_state_(United_States)" title="Free state (United States)">free</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColoradoTerritory_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoTerritory-32">[32]</a></sup> The original boundaries of Colorado remain unchanged today. The name Colorado was chosen because it was commonly believed that the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a> originated in the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colorado_River_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_River-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1776, Spanish priest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silvestre_V%C3%A9lez_de_Escalante" title="Silvestre Vélez de Escalante">Silvestre Vélez de Escalante</a> recorded that <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> in the area knew the river as <i><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rio_Colorado" title="es:Rio Colorado">el Rio Colorado</a></i> for the red-brown silt that the river carried from the mountains.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1859, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topographic</a> expedition led by Captain <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=John_Navarre_Macomb,_Jr.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="John Navarre Macomb, Jr. (page does not exist)">John Macomb</a> located the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_River_(Colorado)" title="Grand River (Colorado)">Grand River</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Canyonlands_National_Park" title="Canyonlands National Park">Canyonlands National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macomb_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macomb-34">[34]</a></sup> The Macomb party designated the confluence as the source of the Colorado River.</p>
<p>On April 12, 1861, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> artillery opened fire on <a href="/wiki/Fort_Sumter" title="Fort Sumter">Fort Sumter</a> to start the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. While many gold seekers held sympathies for the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a>, the vast majority remained fiercely loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> cause.</p>
<p>In 1862, a force of Texas cavalry invaded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Mexico" title="Territory of New Mexico">Territory of New Mexico</a> and captured <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_New_Mexico" title="Santa Fe, New Mexico">Santa Fe</a> on March 10. The object of this <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Campaign" title="New Mexico Campaign">Western Campaign</a> was to seize or disrupt the gold fields of Colorado and California and to seize ports on the Pacific Ocean for the Confederacy. A hastily organized force of Colorado volunteers force-marched from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_City,_Colorado_Territory" title="Denver City, Colorado Territory">Denver City, Colorado Territory</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Glorieta_Pass" title="Glorieta Pass">Glorieta Pass</a>, New Mexico Territory, in an attempt to block the Texans. On March 28, the Coloradans and local New Mexico volunteers stopped the Texans at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Glorieta_Pass" title="Battle of Glorieta Pass">Battle of Glorieta Pass</a>, destroyed their cannon and supply wagons, and dispersed 500 of their horses and mules. The Texans were forced to retreat to Santa Fe. Having lost the supplies for their campaign and finding little support in New Mexico, the Texans abandoned Santa Fe and returned to <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a> in defeat. The Confederacy made no further attempts to seize the Southwestern United States.</p>
<p>In 1864, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Colorado" title="Governor of Colorado">Territorial Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_(governor)" title="John Evans (governor)">John Evans</a> appointed the Reverend <a href="/wiki/John_Chivington" title="John Chivington">John Chivington</a> as Colonel of the Colorado Volunteers with orders to protect white settlers from <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne" title="Cheyenne">Cheyenne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a> warriors who were accused of stealing cattle. Colonel Chivington ordered his men to attack a band of Cheyenne and Arapaho encamped along Sand Creek. Chivington reported that his troops killed more than 500 warriors. The militia returned to Denver City in triumph, but several officers reported that the so-called battle was a blatant massacre of Indians at peace, that most of the dead were women and children, and that bodies of the dead had been hideously mutilated and desecrated. Three U.S. Army inquiries condemned the action, and incoming President <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a> asked Governor Evans for his resignation, but none of the perpetrators was ever punished. This event is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Sand_Creek_massacre" title="Sand Creek massacre">Sand Creek massacre</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="191" data-file-width="250" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg/220px-Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross" title="Mount of the Holy Cross">Mount of the Holy Cross</a> was photographed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Jackson" title="William Henry Jackson">William Henry Jackson</a> in 1874</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the midst and aftermath of Civil War, many discouraged prospectors returned to their homes, but a few stayed and developed mines, mills, farms, ranches, roads, and towns in Colorado Territory. On September 14, 1864, James Huff discovered silver near <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Pass" title="Argentine Pass">Argentine Pass</a>, the first of many silver strikes. In 1867, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a> laid its tracks west to Weir, now <a href="/wiki/Julesburg,_Colorado" title="Julesburg, Colorado">Julesburg</a>, in the northeast corner of the Territory. The Union Pacific linked up with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Railroad" title="Central Pacific Railroad">Central Pacific Railroad</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promontory_Summit,_Utah" title="Promontory Summit, Utah">Promontory Summit, Utah</a>, on May 10, 1869, to form the <a href="/wiki/First_Transcontinental_Railroad" title="First Transcontinental Railroad">First Transcontinental Railroad</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_Pacific_Railway" title="Denver Pacific Railway">Denver Pacific Railway</a> reached Denver in June the following year, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kansas_Pacific" title="Kansas Pacific">Kansas Pacific</a> arrived two months later to forge the second line across the continent. In 1872, rich veins of silver were discovered in the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ute_tribe" title="Ute tribe">Ute Indian</a> reservation in southwestern Colorado. The Ute people were removed from the San Juans the following year.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statehood">Statehood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Statehood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="967" data-file-width="1192" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/220px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/330px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/440px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgetown_Loop" title="Georgetown Loop">Georgetown Loop</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Central_Railroad" title="Colorado Central Railroad">Colorado Central Railroad</a> as photographed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Jackson" title="William Henry Jackson">William Henry Jackson</a> in 1899</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> passed an enabling act on March 3, 1875, specifying the requirements for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a> to become a state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colorado_Enabling_Act_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_Enabling_Act-13">[13]</a></sup> On August 1, 1876 (28 days after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centennial_of_the_United_States" title="Centennial of the United States">Centennial of the United States</a>), U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> signed a proclamation admitting Colorado to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">38th state</a> and earning it the moniker "Centennial State".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colorado_Statehood_Proclamation_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_Statehood_Proclamation-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The discovery of a major silver lode near <a href="/wiki/Leadville,_Colorado" title="Leadville, Colorado">Leadville</a> in 1878 triggered the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Silver_Boom" title="Colorado Silver Boom">Colorado Silver Boom</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Silver_Purchase_Act" title="Sherman Silver Purchase Act">Sherman Silver Purchase Act</a> of 1890 invigorated silver mining, and Colorado's last, but greatest, gold strike at <a href="/wiki/Cripple_Creek,_Colorado" title="Cripple Creek, Colorado">Cripple Creek</a> a few months later lured a new generation of gold seekers. Colorado women were granted the right to vote beginning on November 7, 1893, making Colorado the second state to grant <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> and the first one by a popular vote (of Colorado men). The repeal of the Sherman Silver Purchase Act in 1893 led to a staggering collapse of the mining and agricultural economy of Colorado, but the state slowly and steadily recovered. Between the 1880s and 1930s, Denver's floriculture industry developed into a major industry in Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> This period became known locally as the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Gold_Rush" title="Carnation Gold Rush">Carnation Gold Rush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colorado became the first western state to host a major political convention when the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> met in Denver in 1908. By the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Census,_1930" title="United States Census, 1930">U.S. Census in 1930</a>, the population of Colorado first exceeded one million residents. Colorado suffered greatly through the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl" title="Dust Bowl">Dust Bowl</a> of the 1930s, but a major wave of immigration following World War II boosted Colorado's fortune. Tourism became a mainstay of the state economy, and high technology became an important economic engine. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimated that the population of Colorado exceeded five million in 2009.</p>
<p>Three warships of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> have been named the USS <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado" title="USS Colorado">Colorado</a></i>. The first USS <i>Colorado</i> was named for the Colorado River. The later two ships were named in honor of the state, including the battleship USS <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado_(BB-45)" title="USS Colorado (BB-45)">Colorado</a></i> which served in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_the_Pacific" title="War in the Pacific">World War II in the Pacific</a> beginning in 1941. At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, this USS <i>Colorado</i> was located at the naval base in San Diego, Calif. and hence went unscathed.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">16.9%</td>

<td style="padding-left:8px;">5,540,545</td>
<td style="font-size:85%"></td>
<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">10.2%</td>

<tr>
<td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">Sources: 1910–2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><br/>
2015 estimate<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-10">[10]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Colorado was 5,540,545 on July 1, 2016, a 10.17% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-10">[10]</a></sup> Colorado's most populous city, and capital, is <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora,_CO_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora, CO Combined Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Boulder Combined Statistical Area</a> with an estimated 2013 population of 3,277,309, has 60% of the state's residents.</p>
<p>The largest increases are expected in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Denver_metropolitan_area" title="Denver metropolitan area">Denver metropolitan area</a>. The state's fastest-growing counties are <a href="/wiki/Douglas_County,_Colorado" title="Douglas County, Colorado">Douglas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weld_County,_Colorado" title="Weld County, Colorado">Weld</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Colorado is located just north of the village of Critchell in <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Colorado" title="Jefferson County, Colorado">Jefferson County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, Colorado had a population of 5,029,196. Racial composition of the state's population was:</p>
<ul>
<li>81.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White American</a> (70.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" title="Non-Hispanic White">Non-Hispanic White</a>, 11.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Hispanic" title="White Hispanic">Hispanic white</a>)</li>
<li>20.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanic and Latino American</a> (of any race) heritage</li>
<li>7.2% Some Other Race</li>
<li>4.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a> or African American</li>
<li>3.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Multiracial American</a></li>
<li>2.8% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian American</a></li>
<li>1.1% <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a></li>
<li>0.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" title="Native Hawaiian">Native Hawaiian</a> and Other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a></li>
</ul>

<p>People of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanic and Latino American</a> (of any race made) heritage, made up 20.7% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> According to the 2000 Census, the largest ancestry groups in Colorado are <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German</a> (22%) including of Swiss and <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrian</a> nationalities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American" title="Mexican-American">Mexican</a> (18%), Irish (12%), and English (12%). Persons reporting <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German ancestry</a> are especially numerous in the Front Range, the Rockies (west-central counties) and Eastern parts/High Plains.</p>
<p>Colorado has a high proportion of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>, mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American" title="Mexican-American">Mexican-American</a>, citizens in Metropolitan Denver, Colorado Springs, as well as the smaller cities of Greeley and Pueblo, and elsewhere. Southern, Southwestern, and Southeastern Colorado has a large number of <a href="/wiki/Hispanos" title="Hispanos">Hispanos</a>, the descendants of the early Mexican settlers of colonial Spanish origin. In 1940, the Census Bureau reported Colorado's population as 8.2% Hispanic and 90.3% non-Hispanic white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The Hispanic population of Colorado has continued to grow quickly over the past decades. By 2012, Hispanics made up 21% of Colorado's population, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" title="Non-Hispanic White">Non-Hispanic Whites</a> made up 69%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quickfacts.census.gov_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-quickfacts.census.gov-47">[47]</a></sup> Spoken English in Colorado has many Spanish idioms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colorado also has some large African-American communities located in Denver, in the neighborhoods of Montbello, Five Points, Whittier, and many other East Denver areas. A relatively large population of African Americans are also found in Colorado Springs on the east and southeast side of the city. The state has sizable numbers of Asian-Americans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_American" title="Mongolian American">Mongolian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_American" title="Chinese American">Chinese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_American" title="Filipino American">Filipino</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">Korean</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_American" title="Japanese American">Japanese</a> descent. The highest population of Asian Americans can be found on the south and southeast side of Denver, as well as some on Denver's southwest side. The Denver metropolitan area is considered more liberal and diverse than much of the state when it comes to political issues and environmental concerns.</p>
<p>There were a total of 70,331 births in Colorado in 2006. (Birth rate of 14.6 per thousand.) In 2007, non-Hispanic whites were involved in 59.1% of all the births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Some 14.06% of those births involved a non-Hispanic white person and someone of a different race, most often with a couple including one Hispanic. A birth where at least one Hispanic person was involved counted for 43% of the births in Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>, Colorado has the seventh highest percentage of Hispanics (20.7%) in the U.S. behind <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> (46.3%), <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> (37.6%), <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> (37.6%), <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> (29.6%), <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> (26.5%), and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> (22.5%). Per the 2000 census, the Hispanic population is estimated to be 918,899 or approximately 20% of the state total population. Colorado has the 5th-largest population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-Americans" title="Mexican-Americans">Mexican-Americans</a> behind California, Texas, Arizona, and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>. In percentages, Colorado has the 6th-highest percentage of Mexican-Americans behind New Mexico, California, Texas, Arizona, and Nevada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, 46% of Colorado's population younger than the age of one were minorities, meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Note: Births in table don't add up, because Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race, giving a higher overall number.</i></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Spanish is the second-most spoken language in Colorado, after English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> There is one <a href="/wiki/Native_American_languages_of_Colorado" title="Native American languages of Colorado">Native Coloradan</a> language still spoken in Colorado, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River_Numic_language" title="Colorado River Numic language">Colorado River Numic</a> (Ute).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg/220px-Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg/330px-Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg/440px-Colorado_Rocky_Mtn_Church.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

The Cadet Chapel at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a> near <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major religious affiliations of the people of Colorado are 64% Christian, of whom there are 44% Protestants, 19% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">Roman Catholics</a>, 3% <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">Latter Day Saint</a>/Mormon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> 2% Jews, 1% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, 1% Buddhist and 0.5% Hindu. The religiously unaffiliated make up 25% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest denominations by number of adherents in 2010 were the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> with 811,630; non-denominational Evangelical Protestants with 229,981; and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> with 142,473.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to several studies, Coloradans have the lowest rates of obesity of any state in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 18% of the population was considered medically obese, and while the lowest in the nation, the percentage had increased from 17% in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> According to a report in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Journal_of_the_American_Medical_Association" title="Journal of the American Medical Association">Journal of the American Medical Association</a>, residents of Colorado had a 2014 life expectancy of 80.21 years, the longest of any U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg/220px-Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg/330px-Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg/440px-Denver_Colorado_Art.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fine arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Colorado" title="Music of Colorado">Music of Colorado</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Theater_in_Colorado" title="Theater in Colorado">Theater in Colorado</a></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of film productions have shot on location in Colorado, especially prominent <a href="/wiki/Western_(genre)" title="Western (genre)">Westerns</a> like <i><a href="/wiki/True_Grit_(1969_film)" title="True Grit (1969 film)">True Grit</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Searchers_(film)" title="The Searchers (film)">The Searchers</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Butch_Cassidy_and_the_Sundance_Kid" title="Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid">Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid</a>.</i> A number of historic military forts, railways with trains still operating, mining ghost towns have been utilized and transformed for historical accuracy in well known films. There are also a number of scenic highways and mountain passes that helped to feature the open road in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Vanishing_Point_(1971_film)" title="Vanishing Point (1971 film)">Vanishing Point</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bingo_(1991_film)" title="Bingo (1991 film)">Bingo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Starman_(film)" title="Starman (film)">Starman</a></i>. Some Colorado landmarks have been featured in films, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Stanley_Hotel" title="The Stanley Hotel">The Stanley Hotel</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Dumb_and_Dumber" title="Dumb and Dumber">Dumb and Dumber</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shining_(film)" title="The Shining (film)">The Shining</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Sculptured_House" title="Sculptured House">Sculptured House</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeper_(1973_film)" title="Sleeper (1973 film)">Sleeper</a></i>. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Furious_7" title="Furious 7">Furious 7</a> to film driving sequences <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak_Highway" title="Pikes Peak Highway">Pikes Peak Highway</a> in Colorado. The TV Series, <a href="/wiki/Good_Luck_Charlie" title="Good Luck Charlie">Good Luck Charlie</a> was being filmed in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, Colorado. The Colorado Office of Film and Television has noted that over 400 films have been shot in Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are also a number of established film festivals in Colorado, including <a href="/wiki/Aspen_Shortsfest" title="Aspen Shortsfest">Aspen Shortsfest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boulder_International_Film_Festival" title="Boulder International Film Festival">Boulder International Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Rock_Film_Festival" title="Castle Rock Film Festival">Castle Rock Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denver_Film_Festival" title="Denver Film Festival">Denver Film Festival</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festivus_film_festival" title="Festivus film festival">Festivus film festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mile_High_Horror_Film_Festival" title="Mile High Horror Film Festival">Mile High Horror Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moondance_International_Film_Festival" title="Moondance International Film Festival">Moondance International Film Festival</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountainfilm_in_Telluride" title="Mountainfilm in Telluride">Mountainfilm in Telluride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Women%27s_Film_Festival" title="Rocky Mountain Women's Film Festival">Rocky Mountain Women's Film Festival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telluride_Film_Festival" title="Telluride Film Festival">Telluride Film Festival</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Colorado is known for its <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Southwestern_United_States" title="Cuisine of the Southwestern United States">Southwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_cuisine" title="Rocky Mountain cuisine">Rocky Mountain cuisine</a>. Mexican restaurants are prominent throughout the state.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a> was named America's Foodiest Town 2010 by <a href="/wiki/Bon_App%C3%A9tit" title="Bon Appétit">Bon Appétit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bon_App.C3.A9tit_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bon_App.C3.A9tit-64">[64]</a></sup> Boulder, and Colorado in general, is home to a number of national food and beverage companies, top-tier restaurants and farmers' markets. <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a> also has more Master <a href="/wiki/Sommelier" title="Sommelier">Sommeliers</a> per capita than any other city, including San Francisco and New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denver_Magazine_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denver_Magazine-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_%26_Wine_Classic" title="Food &amp; Wine Classic">Food &amp; Wine Classic</a> is held annually each June in <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen, Colorado</a>. Aspen also has a reputation as the culinary capital of the Rocky Mountain region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> is known for steak, but now has a diverse culinary scene with many restaurants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Travel_.2B_Leisure_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_.2B_Leisure-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wine_and_beer">Wine and beer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Wine and beer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colorado_wine" title="Colorado wine">Colorado wine</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colorado_wine" title="Colorado wine">Colorado wines</a> include award-winning varietals that have attracted favorable notice from outside the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> With wines made from traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Vitis_vinifera" title="Vitis vinifera">Vitis vinifera</a></i> grapes along with wines made from cherries, peaches, plums and honey, Colorado wines have won top national and international awards for their quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jefferson_Cup_Invitational_Wine_Competition_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jefferson_Cup_Invitational_Wine_Competition-69">[69]</a></sup> Colorado's grape growing regions contain the highest elevation <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a> in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> with most <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> in the state practiced between 4,000 and 7,000 feet (1,219 and 2,134 m) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>. The mountain <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> ensures warm summer days and cool nights. Colorado is home to two designated <a href="/wiki/American_Viticultural_Area" title="American Viticultural Area">American Viticultural Areas</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Valley_AVA" title="Grand Valley AVA">Grand Valley AVA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Elks_AVA" title="West Elks AVA">West Elks AVA</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alcohol_and_Tobacco_Tax_and_Trade_Bureau_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alcohol_and_Tobacco_Tax_and_Trade_Bureau-71">[71]</a></sup> where most of the vineyards in the state are located. However, an increasing number of wineries are located along the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colorado_Wine_Industry_Development_Board_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_Wine_Industry_Development_Board-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_beer" title="Colorado beer">Colorado beer</a></div>
<p>Colorado is home to many nationally praised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbreweries" title="Microbreweries">microbreweries</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/New_Belgium_Brewing_Company" title="New Belgium Brewing Company">New Belgium Brewing Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odell_Brewing_Company" title="Odell Brewing Company">Odell Brewing Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Divide_Brewing_Company" title="Great Divide Brewing Company">Great Divide Brewing Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Blues_Brewery" title="Oskar Blues Brewery">Oskar Blues Brewery</a>. The area of northern Colorado near and between the cities of Denver, <a href="/wiki/Boulder" title="Boulder">Boulder</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Collins" title="Fort Collins">Fort Collins</a> is known as the "Napa Valley of Beer" due to its high density of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Craft_breweries" title="Craft breweries">craft breweries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Denver_Beer_Triangle_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Denver_Beer_Triangle-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marijuana_and_hemp">Marijuana and hemp</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Marijuana and hemp">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Colorado is open to pot tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> With the adoption of their <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Amendment_64" title="Colorado Amendment 64">64th state amendment</a> In 2013 Colorado became the first state in the union to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legality_of_cannabis_by_US_state" title="Legality of cannabis by US state">legalize</a> the <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis_in_the_United_States#Colorado" title="Medical cannabis in the United States">medicinal</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">industrial</a> (2013), and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Amendment_64" title="Colorado Amendment 64">recreational</a> (2014) use of marijuana. Colorado's marijuana industry sold 996 million dollars worth of marijuana in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Colorado regulates hemp as any part of the plant with less than 0.03% THC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amendment 64, adopted by the voters in the 2014 general election, forces the Colorado state legislature to enact legislation governing the cultivation, processing and sale of recreational marijuana and industrial hemp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On April 4, 2014 Senate Bill 14–184 addressing oversight of Colorado's industrial hemp program was first introduced, ultimately being signed into law by Governor John Hickenlooper on May 31, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicinal_use">Medicinal use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Medicinal use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On November 7, 2000, 54% of Colorado voters passed Amendment 20, which amends the Colorado State constitution to allow the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_use_of_cannabis" title="Medical use of cannabis">medical use of marijuana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norml-co_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-norml-co-80">[80]</a></sup> A patient's medical use of marijuana, within the following limits, is lawful:</p>
<ul>
<li>(I) No more than 2 ounces (57 g) of a usable form of marijuana; and</li>
<li>(II) No more than twelve marijuana plants, with six or fewer being mature, flowering plants that are producing a usable form of marijuana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Currently Colorado has listed "eight medical conditions for which patients can use marijuana—cancer, glaucoma, HIV/AIDS, muscle spasms, seizures, severe pain, severe nausea and cachexia, or dramatic weight loss and muscle atrophy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Young_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Young-82">[82]</a></sup> Colorado Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Hickenlooper" title="John Hickenlooper">John Hickenlooper</a> has allocated about half of the state's $13 million "Medical Marijuana Program Cash Fund"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMPCF_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMPCF-83">[83]</a></sup> to medical research in the 2014 budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markus_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Markus-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational_use">Recreational use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Recreational use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On November 6, 2012, voters amended the state constitution to protect <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Amendment_64" title="Colorado Amendment 64">"personal use" of marijuana for adults</a>, establishing a framework to regulate <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a> in a manner similar to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The first recreational marijuana shops in Colorado, and by extension the United States, opened their doors on January 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Healy_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Healy-87">[87]</a></sup> In Colorado marijuana sales generate high amounts of tax money to be used for repairs, schools etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Colorado" title="Sports in Colorado">Sports in Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado has five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_league" title="Major professional sports league">major professional sports leagues</a>, all based in the Denver metropolitan area. Colorado is the least populous state with a franchise in each of the major professional sports leagues.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak_International_Hill_Climb" title="Pikes Peak International Hill Climb">Pikes Peak International Hill Climb</a> is a major hillclimbing motor race held at the Pikes Peak Highway.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hills_Country_Club" title="Cherry Hills Country Club">Cherry Hills Country Club</a> has hosted several professional golf tournaments, including the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senior_Open" title="U.S. Senior Open">U.S. Senior Open</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Women%27s_Open" title="U.S. Women's Open">U.S. Women's Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW_Championship_(PGA_Tour)" title="BMW Championship (PGA Tour)">BMW Championship</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="College_athletics">College athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: College athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_Colorado" title="List of college athletic programs in Colorado">List of college athletic programs in Colorado</a></div>
<p>The following universities and colleges participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a>. The most popular college sports program is the University of Colorado Buffaloes, who used to play in the Big-12 but now play in the Pac-12. They have won the 1957 and 1991 <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl" title="Orange Bowl">Orange Bowl</a>, 1995 <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Bowl" title="Fiesta Bowl">Fiesta Bowl</a> and 1996 <a href="/wiki/Cotton_Bowl_Classic" title="Cotton Bowl Classic">Cotton Bowl Classic</a>.</p>
