<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/170px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/255px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/340px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Denver Energy Center<br/>
The Denver financial district along 17th Street is known as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_Street_of_the_West" title="Wall Street of the West">Wall Street of the West</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colorado" title="Economy of Colorado">Economy of Colorado</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Colorado locations by per capita income">Colorado locations by per capita income</a></div>
<p>CNBC's list of "Top States for Business for 2010" has recognized Colorado as the third-best state in the nation, falling short to only Texas and Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="2700" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/220px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/330px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/440px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Corn</a> growing in <a href="/wiki/Larimer_County,_Colorado" title="Larimer County, Colorado">Larimer County</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The total state product in 2015 was $318,600 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_GDP_per_capita_(nominal)" title="List of U.S. states by GDP per capita (nominal)">Per capita personal income</a> in 2010 was $51 940, ranking Colorado 11th in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The state's economy broadened from its mid-19th-century roots in mining when irrigated agriculture developed, and by the late 19th century, raising livestock had become important. Early industry was based on the extraction and processing of minerals and agricultural products. Current agricultural products are cattle, wheat, <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">hay</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal government</a> is also a major economic force in the state with many important federal facilities including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NORAD" title="NORAD">NORAD</a> (North American Aerospace Defense Command), <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a>, Schriever Air Force Base located approximately 10 miles (16 kilometers) east of <a href="/wiki/Peterson_Air_Force_Base" title="Peterson Air Force Base">Peterson Air Force Base</a>, and Fort Carson, both located in <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a> within El Paso County; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>, the National Renewable Energy Laboratory (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NREL" title="NREL">NREL</a>) in Golden, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Geological_Survey" title="U.S. Geological Survey">U.S. Geological Survey</a> and other government agencies at the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Federal_Center" title="Denver Federal Center">Denver Federal Center</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lakewood,_Colorado" title="Lakewood, Colorado">Lakewood</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Mint" title="Denver Mint">Denver Mint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buckley_Air_Force_Base" title="Buckley Air Force Base">Buckley Air Force Base</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Tenth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit">Tenth Circuit Court of Appeals</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Byron_G._Rogers_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse">Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse</a> in Denver; and a federal <a href="/wiki/ADX_Florence" title="ADX Florence">Supermax Prison</a> and other federal prisons near <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1on_City,_Colorado" title="Cañon City, Colorado">Cañon City</a>. In addition to these and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_Agencies_of_the_United_States_Government" title="Independent Agencies of the United States Government">federal agencies</a>, Colorado has abundant <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Forest" title="United States National Forest">National Forest</a> land and four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_National_Parks_of_the_United_States" title="List of National Parks of the United States">National Parks</a> that contribute to federal ownership of 24,615,788 acres (99,617 km<sup>2</sup>) of land in Colorado, or 37% of the total area of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In the second half of the 20th century, the industrial and service sectors have expanded greatly. The state's economy is diversified and is notable for its concentration of scientific research and high-technology industries. Other industries include <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, transportation equipment, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">machinery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical products</a>, the extraction of metals such as gold (see <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining_in_Colorado" title="Gold mining in Colorado">Gold mining in Colorado</a>), silver, and <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>. Colorado now also has the largest annual production of beer of any state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Denver is an important financial center.</p>
<p>A number of nationally known brand names have originated in Colorado factories and laboratories. From <a href="/wiki/Denver#Economy" title="Denver">Denver</a> came the forerunner of telecommunications giant <a href="/wiki/Qwest_Corporation" title="Qwest Corporation">Qwest</a> in 1879, <a href="/wiki/Samsonite" title="Samsonite">Samsonite</a> luggage in 1910, <a href="/wiki/Gates_Corporation" title="Gates Corporation">Gates</a> belts and hoses in 1911, and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Stover_Candies" title="Russell Stover Candies">Russell Stover Candies</a> in 1923. Kuner canned vegetables began in <a href="/wiki/Brighton,_Colorado" title="Brighton, Colorado">Brighton</a> in 1864. From <a href="/wiki/Golden,_Colorado" title="Golden, Colorado">Golden</a> came <a href="/wiki/Coors_Brewing_Company" title="Coors Brewing Company">Coors</a> beer in 1873, <a href="/wiki/CoorsTek" title="CoorsTek">CoorsTek</a> industrial ceramics in 1920, and <a href="/wiki/Jolly_Rancher" title="Jolly Rancher">Jolly Rancher</a> candy in 1949. <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Fuel_and_Iron" title="Colorado Fuel and Iron">CF&amp;I</a> railroad rails, wire, nails and pipe debuted in <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo</a> in 1892. <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Sugar" title="Imperial Sugar">Holly Sugar</a> was first milled from beets in <a href="/wiki/Holly,_Colorado" title="Holly, Colorado">Holly</a> in 1905, and later moved its headquarters to Colorado Springs. The present-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swift_%26_Company" title="Swift &amp; Company">Swift</a> packed meat of <a href="/wiki/Greeley,_Colorado" title="Greeley, Colorado">Greeley</a> evolved from Monfort of Colorado, Inc., established in 1930. <a href="/wiki/Estes_Industries" title="Estes Industries">Estes</a> model rockets were launched in <a href="/wiki/Penrose,_Colorado" title="Penrose, Colorado">Penrose</a> in 1958. <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins</a> has been the home of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodward_Governor_Company" title="Woodward Governor Company">Woodward Governor Company</a>'s motor controllers (governors) since 1870, and <a href="/wiki/Oral_irrigator" title="Oral irrigator">Waterpik</a> dental water jets and showerheads since 1962. <a href="/wiki/Celestial_Seasonings" title="Celestial Seasonings">Celestial Seasonings</a> herbal teas have been made in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a> since 1969. <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Chocolate_Factory" title="Rocky Mountain Chocolate Factory">Rocky Mountain Chocolate Factory</a> made its first candy in <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Colorado" title="Durango, Colorado">Durango</a> in 1981.</p>
<p>Colorado has a flat 4.63% <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, regardless of income level. Unlike most states, which calculate taxes based on federal <i>adjusted gross income</i>, Colorado taxes are based on <i>taxable income</i>—income after federal exemptions and federal itemized (or standard) deductions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Colorado's state <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> is 2.9% on retail sales. When state revenues exceed state constitutional limits, according to Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Taxpayer_Bill_of_Rights" title="Taxpayer Bill of Rights">Taxpayer Bill of Rights</a> legislation, full-year Colorado residents can claim a sales tax refund on their individual state income tax return. Many counties and cities charge their own rates in addition to the base state rate. There are also certain county and special district taxes that may apply.</p>
<p>Real estate and personal business property are taxable in Colorado. The state's senior property tax exemption was temporarily suspended by the Colorado Legislature in 2003. The tax break is scheduled to return for assessment year 2006, payable in 2007.</p>
<p>As of August 2014, the state's unemployment rate is 5.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Major philanthropic organizations based in Colorado include the <a href="/wiki/Daniels_Fund" title="Daniels Fund">Daniels Fund</a>, the Anschutz Family Foundation, the <a href="/wiki/Gates_Family_Foundation" title="Gates Family Foundation">Gates Family Foundation</a>, the El Pomar Foundation and the <a href="/wiki/Boettcher_Foundation" title="Boettcher Foundation">Boettcher Foundation</a> grant each year from approximately $7 billion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> of assets.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/220px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/330px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/440px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">oil well</a> in western Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Colorado has significant <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> resources. According to the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a>, Colorado hosts seven of the Nation's 100 largest natural gas fields and two of its 100 largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">oil fields</a>. Conventional and unconventional natural gas output from several Colorado basins typically account for more than 5 percent of annual U.S. natural gas production. Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> deposits hold an estimated 1 trillion barrels (160 km<sup>3</sup>) of oil—nearly as much oil as the entire world's proven oil reserves; the economic viability of the oil shale, however, has not been demonstrated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Substantial deposits of <a href="/wiki/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">bituminous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sub-bituminous_coal" title="Sub-bituminous coal">subbituminous</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> coal are found in the state.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining_in_Colorado" title="Uranium mining in Colorado">Uranium mining in Colorado</a> goes back to 1872, when pitchblende ore was taken from gold mines near Central City, Colorado. The Colorado uranium industry has seen booms and busts, but continues to this day. Not counting byproduct uranium from phosphate, Colorado is considered to have the third largest uranium reserves of any US state, behind Wyoming and New Mexico.</p>
<p>Uranium price increases from 2001 to 2007 prompted a number of companies to revive uranium mining in Colorado. However, price drops and financing problems in late 2008 forced these companies to cancel or scale back uranium-mining projects. There are no currently producing uranium mines in Colorado.</p>
<p>Colorado's high Rocky Mountain ridges and eastern plains offer <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> potential, and geologic activity in the mountain areas provides potential for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geothermal_electricity" title="Geothermal electricity">geothermal power</a> development. Much of the state is sunny and could produce <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Colorado" title="Solar power in Colorado">solar power</a>. Major rivers flowing from the Rocky Mountains offer <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric power</a> resources. Corn grown in the flat eastern part of the state offers potential resources for <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a> production.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Colorado" title="Transportation in Colorado">Transportation in Colorado</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colorado.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1235" data-file-width="1730" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Colorado.JPG/220px-Colorado.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Colorado.JPG/330px-Colorado.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Colorado.JPG/440px-Colorado.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colorado.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Colorado state welcome sign</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Colorado's primary mode of transportation (in terms of passengers) is its highway system. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_25_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 25 in Colorado">Interstate 25</a> (I-25) is the primary north–south highway in the state, connecting Pueblo, Colorado Springs, Denver, and Fort Collins, and extending north to Wyoming and south to New Mexico. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 70 in Colorado">I-70</a> is the primary east–west corridor. It connects Grand Junction and the mountain communities with Denver, and enters Utah and Kansas. The state is home to a network of US and Colorado highways that provide access to all principal areas of the state. Many smaller communities are only connected to this network via county roads.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/220px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/330px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/440px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The main terminal of Denver International Airport evokes the peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a> (DIA) is the fourth-busiest domestic U.S. airport and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">thirteenth-busiest world airport</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> DIA handles by far the largest volume of commercial air traffic in Colorado, and is the busiest U.S. hub airport between Chicago and the Pacific coast, making Denver the most important airport for connecting passenger traffic in the western United States.</p>
<p>Extensive public transportation bus services are offered both intra-city and inter-city—including the Denver metro area's extensive RTD services. The <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> (RTD) operates the popular <a href="/wiki/RTD_Bus_%26_Rail" title="RTD Bus &amp; Rail">RTD Bus &amp; Rail</a> transit system in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_Metropolitan_Area" title="Denver Metropolitan Area">Denver Metropolitan Area</a>. As of January 2013 the RTD rail system had 170 light-rail vehicles, serving 47 miles (76 km) of track.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/220px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/330px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/440px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The westbound and eastbound <i><a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyrs</a></i> meet in the <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Canyon" title="Glenwood Canyon">Glenwood Canyon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> operates two passenger rail lines in Colorado, the <a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Chief" title="Southwest Chief">Southwest Chief</a>. Colorado's contribution to world railroad history was forged principally by the <a href="/wiki/Denver_and_Rio_Grande_Western_Railroad" title="Denver and Rio Grande Western Railroad">Denver and Rio Grande Western Railroad</a> which began in 1870 and wrote the book on mountain railroading. In 1988 the "Rio Grande" acquired, but was merged into, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Pacific_Railroad" title="Southern Pacific Railroad">Southern Pacific Railroad</a> by their joint owner <a href="/wiki/Philip_Anschutz" title="Philip Anschutz">Philip Anschutz</a>. On September 11, 1996, Anschutz sold the combined company to the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a>, creating the largest railroad network in the United States. The Anschutz sale was partly in response to the earlier merger of Burlington Northern and Santa Fe which formed the large Burlington Northern and Santa Fe Railway (BNSF), Union Pacific's principal competitor in western U.S. railroading. Both Union Pacific and BNSF have extensive freight operations in Colorado.</p>
<p>Colorado's freight railroad network consists of 2,688 miles of Class I trackage. It is integral to the U.S. economy, being a critical artery for the movement of energy, agriculture, mining, and industrial commodities as well as general freight and manufactured products between the East and Midwest and the Pacific coast states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>In August 2014, Colorado began to issue driver licenses to <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">aliens</a> <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">not lawfully in the United States</a> who lived in Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In September 2014, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KCNC" title="KCNC">KCNC</a> reported that 524 non-citizens were issued licenses issued to U.S. citizens living in Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_government">State government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: State government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Colorado" title="Political party strength in Colorado">Political party strength in Colorado</a></div>
<p>Like the federal government and all other U.S. states, Colorado's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_State_of_Colorado" title="Constitution of the State of Colorado">state constitution</a> provides for three branches of government: the legislative, the executive, and the judicial branches.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Colorado" title="Governor of Colorado">Governor of Colorado</a> heads the state's executive branch. The current governor is <a href="/wiki/John_Hickenlooper" title="John Hickenlooper">John Hickenlooper</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a>. Colorado's other statewide elected executive officers are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Colorado" title="Lieutenant Governor of Colorado">Lieutenant Governor of Colorado</a> (elected on a <a href="/wiki/Ticket_(election)" title="Ticket (election)">ticket</a> with the Governor), <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Colorado" title="Secretary of State of Colorado">Secretary of State of Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_Treasurer" title="Colorado State Treasurer">Colorado State Treasurer</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Colorado" title="Attorney General of Colorado">Attorney General of Colorado</a>, all of whom serve four-year terms.</p>
<div style="clear:right;"></div>

</tr>
</table>
<p>The seven-member <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Supreme_Court" title="Colorado Supreme Court">Colorado Supreme Court</a> is the highest judicial court in the state. The state legislative body is the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_General_Assembly" title="Colorado General Assembly">Colorado General Assembly</a>, which is made up of two houses, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_House_of_Representatives" title="Colorado House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Senate" title="Colorado Senate">Senate</a>. The House has 65 members and the Senate has 35. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican Party</a> holds an 18 to 17 majority in the Senate and a 31 to 34 minority in the House.</p>
<p>Most Coloradans are native to other states (nearly 60% according to the 2000 census),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> and this is illustrated by the fact that the state did not have a native-born governor from 1975 (when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_David_Vanderhoof" title="John David Vanderhoof">John David Vanderhoof</a> left office) until 2007, when Bill Ritter took office; <a href="/wiki/Colorado_gubernatorial_election,_2006" title="Colorado gubernatorial election, 2006">his election</a> the previous year marked the first electoral victory for a native-born Coloradan in a gubernatorial race since 1958 (Vanderhoof had ascended from the Lieutenant Governorship when <a href="/wiki/John_Arthur_Love" title="John Arthur Love">John Arthur Love</a> was given a position in <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>'s administration in 1973). In the 2016 election, the Democratic party won the Colorado electoral college votes.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Colorado_counties,_labelled.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4511" data-file-width="6233" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg/220px-Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg/330px-Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg/440px-Map_of_Colorado_counties%2C_labelled.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Colorado_counties,_labelled.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An enlargeable map of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Colorado" title="List of counties in Colorado">64 counties</a> of the State of Colorado</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Colorado" title="List of counties in Colorado">List of counties in Colorado</a></div>
<p>The State of Colorado is divided into 64 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountiesCO_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-CountiesCO-109">[109]</a></sup> Counties are important units of government in Colorado since the state has no secondary civil subdivisions such as <a href="/wiki/Township_(United_States)" title="Township (United States)">townships</a>. Two of these counties, the <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">City and County of Denver</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Broomfield,_Colorado" title="Broomfield, Colorado">City and County of Broomfield</a>, have <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated city and county governments</a>.</p>
<p>Nine Colorado counties have a population in excess of 250,000 each, while eight Colorado counties have a population of less than 2,500 each. The ten most populous Colorado counties are all located in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_areas">Metropolitan areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Metropolitan areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="829" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg/220px-Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg/330px-Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg/440px-Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colorado_census_statistical_areas.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the 14 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">Core Based Statistical Areas</a> in the state of Colorado.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colorado_metropolitan_areas" title="Colorado metropolitan areas">Colorado metropolitan areas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_census_statistical_areas" title="Colorado census statistical areas">Colorado census statistical areas</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a> (OMB) has defined one <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">combined statistical area</a> (CSA),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSA_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSA-110">[110]</a></sup> seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">Metropolitan Statistical Areas</a> (MSAs),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSA_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSA-111">[111]</a></sup> and seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Micropolitan Statistical Area">Micropolitan Statistical Areas</a> (μSAs)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.CE.BCSA_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-.CE.BCSA-112">[112]</a></sup> in the state of Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMB_10-02_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-OMB_10-02-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most populous of the 14 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">Core Based Statistical Areas</a> in Colorado is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Broomfield,_CO_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Broomfield, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Broomfield, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>. This area had an estimated population of 2,599,504 on July 1, 2011, an increase of +2.20% since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AF_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-AF-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>The more extensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Boulder,_CO_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Boulder, CO Combined Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Boulder, CO Combined Statistical Area</a> had an estimated population of 3,157,520 on July 1, 2011, an increase of +2.16% since the 2010 United States Census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AF_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-AF-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most populous extended metropolitan region in Rocky Mountain Region is the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a> along the northeast face of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a>. This region with <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> at its center had an estimated population of 4,495,181 on July 1, 2012, an increase of +3.73% since the 2010 United States Census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AF_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-AF-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Colorado" title="List of cities and towns in Colorado">List of cities and towns in Colorado</a></div>
<p>The state of Colorado currently has 271 active <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">incorporated municipalities</a>, including 196 towns, 73 cities, and two consolidated city and county governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COmuniStatus_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-COmuniStatus-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COgovTypes_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-COgovTypes-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colorado municipalities operate under one of five types of municipal governing authority. Colorado has one town with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities#Territorial_charter_municipality" title="Colorado municipalities">territorial charter</a>, 160 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities#Statutory_town" title="Colorado municipalities">statutory towns</a>, 12 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities#Statutory_city" title="Colorado municipalities">statutory cities</a>, 96 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities#Home_rule_municipality" title="Colorado municipalities">home rule municipalities</a> (61 cities and 35 towns), and 2 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities#Consolidated_city_and_county" title="Colorado municipalities">consolidated city and county governments</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:855px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg" title="The skyline of downtown Denver with Speer Boulevard in the foreground"><img alt="" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="2048" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg/847px-2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg/1271px-2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg/1694px-2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg 2x" width="847"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2006-07-14-Denver_Skyline_Midnight.jpg" title="File:2006-07-14-Denver Skyline Midnight.jpg"></a></div>
The skyline of downtown <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> with Speer Boulevard in the foreground</div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unincorporated_communities">Unincorporated communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Unincorporated communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Places_in_Colorado" title="Places in Colorado">Places in Colorado</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_districts">Special districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Special districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The state of Colorado has more than 3,000 districts with taxing authority. These districts may provide schools, law enforcement, fire protection, water, sewage, drainage, irrigation, transportation, recreation, infrastructure, cultural facilities, business support, redevelopment, or other services.</p>
<p>Some of these districts have authority to levy sales tax and well as property tax and use fees. This has led to a hodgepodge of sales tax and property tax rates in Colorado. There are some street intersections in Colorado with a different sales tax rate on each corner, sometimes substantially different.</p>
<p>Some of the more notable Colorado districts are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> (RTD), which affects the counties of Denver, Boulder, Jefferson, and portions of Adams, Arapahoe, Broomfield, and Douglas Counties</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Scientific_and_Cultural_Facilities_District" title="Scientific and Cultural Facilities District">Scientific and Cultural Facilities District</a> (SCFD), a special regional tax district with physical boundaries contiguous with county boundaries of Adams, Arapahoe, Boulder, Broomfield, Denver, Douglas, and Jefferson Counties
<ul>
<li>It is a 0.1% retail sales and use tax (one penny on every $10).</li>
<li>According to the Colorado statute, the SCFD distributes the money to local organizations on an annual basis. These organizations must provide for the enlightenment and entertainment of the public through the production, presentation, exhibition, advancement or preservation of art, music, theater, dance, zoology, botany, natural history or cultural history.</li>
<li>As directed by statute, SCFD recipient organizations are currently divided into three "tiers" among which receipts are allocated by percentage.
<ul>
<li>Tier I includes regional organizations: the Denver Art Museum, the Denver Botanic Gardens, the Denver Museum of Nature and Science, the Denver Zoo, and the Denver Center for the Performing Arts. It receives 65.5%.</li>
<li>Tier II currently includes 26 regional organizations. Tier II receives 21%.</li>
<li>Tier III has over 280 local organizations such as small theaters, orchestras, art centers, and natural history, cultural history, and community groups. Tier III organizations apply for funding to the county cultural councils via a grant process. This tier receives 13.5%.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>An 11-member board of directors oversees the distributions in accordance with the Colorado Revised Statutes. Seven board members are appointed by county commissioners (in Denver, the Denver City Council) and four members are appointed by the Governor of Colorado.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The Football Stadium District (FD or FTBL), approved by the voters to pay for and help build the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>' stadium <a href="/wiki/Sports_Authority_Field_at_Mile_High" title="Sports Authority Field at Mile High">Sports Authority Field at Mile High</a></li>
<li>Local Improvement Districts (LID) within designated areas of southeast Jefferson and Boulder counties</li>
<li>The Metropolitan Major League Baseball Stadium District, approved by voters to pay for and help build the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>' stadium <a href="/wiki/Coors_Field" title="Coors Field">Coors Field</a></li>
<li>Regional Transportation Authority (RTA) taxes at varying rates in Basalt, Carbondale, Glenwood Springs, Gunnison County</li>
</ul>

<p>Colorado is considered a <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a> in both state and federal elections. Coloradans have elected 17 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> and 12 <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> to the governorship in the last 100 years. In presidential politics, Colorado was considered a reliably Republican state during the post-World War II era, only voting for the Democratic candidate in 1948, 1964, and 1992. However, it became a competitive swing state by the turn of the century, and voted consecutively for Democrat Barack Obama in 2008 and 2012, as well as Democrat Hillary Clinton in 2016.</p>
<p>Colorado politics has the contrast of conservative cities such as Colorado Springs and liberal cities such as Boulder and Denver. Democrats are strongest in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_Metropolitan_Area" title="Denver Metropolitan Area">metropolitan Denver</a>, the college towns of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>, southern Colorado (including Pueblo), and a few western ski resort counties. The Republicans are strongest in the Eastern Plains, Colorado Springs, Greeley, and far Western Colorado near Grand Junction.</p>
<p>The state of Colorado is represented by its two <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senators</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Classes_of_United_States_Senators" title="Classes of United States Senators">United States Senate Class 2</a> – <a href="/wiki/Cory_Gardner" title="Cory Gardner">Cory Gardner</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>) 2015–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Classes_of_United_States_Senators" title="Classes of United States Senators">United States Senate Class 3</a> – <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bennet" title="Michael Bennet">Michael Bennet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>) 2009–</li>
</ul>
<p>Colorado is represented by seven <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">Representatives</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 1st congressional district">Colorado's 1st congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Diana_DeGette" title="Diana DeGette">Diana DeGette</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>) 1997–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 2nd congressional district">Colorado's 2nd congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Jared_Polis" title="Jared Polis">Jared Polis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>) 2009–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 3rd congressional district">Colorado's 3rd congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Scott_Tipton" title="Scott Tipton">Scott Tipton</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>) 2011–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 4th congressional district">Colorado's 4th congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ken_Buck" title="Ken Buck">Ken Buck</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>) 2015–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 5th congressional district">Colorado's 5th congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Doug_Lamborn" title="Doug Lamborn">Doug Lamborn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>) 2007–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 6th congressional district">Colorado's 6th congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mike_Coffman" title="Mike Coffman">Mike Coffman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>) 2009–</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_7th_congressional_district" title="Colorado's 7th congressional district">Colorado's 7th congressional district</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ed_Perlmutter" title="Ed Perlmutter">Ed Perlmutter</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>) 2007–</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Significant_bills_passed_in_Colorado">Significant bills passed in Colorado</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Significant bills passed in Colorado">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the November 8, 1932 ballot, Colorado approved the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Repeal_of_Prohibition" title="Repeal of Prohibition">repeal of alcohol prohibition</a> more than a year before the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-first_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-first Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-first Amendment to the United States Constitution</a> was ratified.</p>
<p>In 2012, voters amended the state constitution protecting <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Amendment_64" title="Colorado Amendment 64">"personal use" of marijuana for adults</a>, establishing a framework to regulate <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> in a manner similar to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a>. The first recreational marijuana shops in Colorado, and by extension the United States, opened their doors on January 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Healy_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Healy-87">[87]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_installations">Military installations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Military installations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carsongate.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/220px-Carsongate.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/330px-Carsongate.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/440px-Carsongate.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<p>Colorado is currently the home of seven major military bases and installations.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Reserve_Personnel_Center" title="Air Reserve Personnel Center">Air Reserve Personnel Center</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buckley_Air_Force_Base" title="Buckley Air Force Base">Buckley Air Force Base</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Carson" title="Fort Carson">Fort Carson</a> (U.S. Army)
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pi%C3%B1on_Canyon_Maneuver_Site" title="Piñon Canyon Maneuver Site">Piñon Canyon Maneuver Site</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peterson_Air_Force_Base" title="Peterson Air Force Base">Peterson Air Force Base</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Mountain_Division" title="Cheyenne Mountain Division">Cheyenne Mountain Division</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Chemical_Depot" title="Pueblo Chemical Depot">Pueblo Chemical Depot</a> (U.S. Army)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schriever_Air_Force_Base" title="Schriever Air Force Base">Schriever Air Force Base</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Former Military installations and outposts include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Camp_Collins" title="Camp Collins">Camp Collins</a> (1862–1870)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Camp_Hale" title="Camp Hale">Camp Hale</a> (1942–1945)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fitzsimons_Army_Medical_Center" title="Fitzsimons Army Medical Center">Fitzsimons Army Hospital</a> (1918–1999)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Garland" title="Fort Garland">Fort Garland</a> (1858–1883)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Logan" title="Fort Logan">Fort Logan</a> (1887–1946)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lowry_Air_Force_Base" title="Lowry Air Force Base">Lowry Air Force Base</a> (1938–1994)</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="275" data-file-width="400" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg/220px-Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg/330px-Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Lowry_Pueblo_ruins.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coloradodunes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="750" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Coloradodunes.jpg/220px-Coloradodunes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Coloradodunes.jpg/330px-Coloradodunes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Coloradodunes.jpg/440px-Coloradodunes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="1750" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg/220px-SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg/330px-SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg/440px-SpruceTreeHouseLong.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Spruce Tree House in <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde National Park</a></div>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_lands_in_Colorado" title="List of federal lands in Colorado">List of federal lands in Colorado</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_State_Parks" title="Colorado State Parks">Colorado State Parks</a></div>
<p>Colorado is home to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Colorado" title="List of national parks in Colorado">4 national parks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_monuments_of_Colorado" title="National monuments of Colorado">8 national monuments</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_recreation_areas_of_Colorado" title="National recreation areas of Colorado">2 national recreation areas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_historic_sites_of_Colorado" title="National historic sites of Colorado">2 national historic sites</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_historic_trails_of_Colorado" title="National historic trails of Colorado">3 national historic trails</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_scenic_trail_of_Colorado" title="National scenic trail of Colorado">a national scenic trail</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_forests_of_Colorado" title="National forests of Colorado">11 national forests</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_grasslands_of_Colorado" title="National grasslands of Colorado">2 national grasslands</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_wilderness_areas_of_Colorado" title="National wilderness areas of Colorado">42 national wilderness areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_lands_in_Colorado#National_Conservation_Areas" title="List of federal lands in Colorado">2 national conservation areas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_wildlife_refuges_of_Colorado" title="National wildlife refuges of Colorado">8 national wildlife refuges</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colorado_state_parks" title="List of Colorado state parks">44 state parks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_Division_of_Wildlife" title="Colorado Division of Wildlife">307 state wildlife areas</a>, and numerous other scenic, historic, and recreational areas.</p>
<p>Units of the National Park System in Colorado:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arapaho_National_Recreation_Area" title="Arapaho National Recreation Area">Arapaho National Recreation Area</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFS_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-NFS-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bent%27s_Old_Fort_National_Historic_Site" title="Bent's Old Fort National Historic Site">Bent's Old Fort National Historic Site</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black_Canyon_of_the_Gunnison_National_Park" title="Black Canyon of the Gunnison National Park">Black Canyon of the Gunnison National Park</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Browns_Canyon_National_Monument" title="Browns Canyon National Monument">Browns Canyon National Monument</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLMNFS_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLMNFS-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canyons_of_the_Ancients_National_Monument" title="Canyons of the Ancients National Monument">Canyons of the Ancients National Monument</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLM_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLM-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chimney_Rock_National_Monument" title="Chimney Rock National Monument">Chimney Rock National Monument</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFS_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-NFS-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado_National_Monument" title="Colorado National Monument">Colorado National Monument</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_National_Scenic_Trail" title="Continental Divide National Scenic Trail">Continental Divide National Scenic Trail</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFSNPSBLM_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-NFSNPSBLM-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Curecanti_National_Recreation_Area" title="Curecanti National Recreation Area">Curecanti National Recreation Area</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dinosaur_National_Monument" title="Dinosaur National Monument">Dinosaur National Monument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Florissant_Fossil_Beds_National_Monument" title="Florissant Fossil Beds National Monument">Florissant Fossil Beds National Monument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Sand_Dunes_National_Park_and_Preserve" title="Great Sand Dunes National Park and Preserve">Great Sand Dunes National Park and Preserve</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hovenweep_National_Monument" title="Hovenweep National Monument">Hovenweep National Monument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde National Park</a> and UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_National_Historic_Trail" title="Old Spanish National Historic Trail">Old Spanish National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pony_Express_National_Historic_Trail" title="Pony Express National Historic Trail">Pony Express National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_National_Park" title="Rocky Mountain National Park">Rocky Mountain National Park</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sand_Creek_Massacre_National_Historic_Site" title="Sand Creek Massacre National Historic Site">Sand Creek Massacre National Historic Site</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_National_Historic_Trail" title="Santa Fe National Historic Trail">Santa Fe National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yucca_House_National_Monument" title="Yucca House National Monument">Yucca House National Monument</a></li>
</ul>

<li id="cite_note-Colorado_River-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Colorado_River_33-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Early explorers identified the <a href="/wiki/Gunnison_River" title="Gunnison River">Gunnison River</a> in Colorado as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Headwaters" title="Headwaters">headwaters</a> of the Colorado River. The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Grand River</a> in Colorado was later tentatively identified as the primary headwaters of the river. Finally in 1916, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=E.C._LaRue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="E.C. LaRue (page does not exist)">E.C. LaRue</a>, the Chief Hydrologist of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a>, identified the Green River in southwestern Wyoming as the proper headwaters of the actual, overall Colorado River.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Macomb-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Macomb_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Report of the exploring expedition from Santa Fé, New Mexico, to the junction of the Grand and Green Rivers of the great Colorado of the West, in 1859: under the command of Capt. J. N. Macomb, Corps of topographical engineers, Volume 1 <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/reportofexplorin00unitrich#page/n5/mode/2up" rel="nofollow">@ archive.org</a></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Air Force teams participate in other conferences, or as independents, in sports that the MW does not sponsor:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">Boxing, a men-only sport which is not sanctioned by the NCAA, competes as an independent.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Fencing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, also competes as an independent.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's and women's gymnastics both compete in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's ice hockey competes in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Hockey" title="Atlantic Hockey">Atlantic Hockey</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's lacrosse competes in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Conference" title="Southern Conference">Southern Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Rifle, which at Air Force is a coeducational sport, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_Rifle_Conference" title="Patriot Rifle Conference">Patriot Rifle Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's soccer and women's swimming &amp; diving compete in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Wrestling, a men-only sport, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Colorado teams participate in other conferences in sports that the Pac-12 does not sponsor:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">Women's lacrosse and men's and women's indoor track &amp; field all competes in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Skiing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Intercollegiate_Ski_Association" title="Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association">Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association</a>.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Denver teams participate in other conferences in sports that The Summit League does not sponsor:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">Women's gymnastics competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's ice hockey competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Hockey_Conference" title="National Collegiate Hockey Conference">National Collegiate Hockey Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Men's and women's lacrosse compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Skiing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Intercollegiate_Ski_Association" title="Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association">Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association</a>.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Northern Colorado teams participate in other conferences in sports that the Big Sky does not sponsor:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">Baseball (a men-only sport) and women's swimming &amp; diving compete in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a>.</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Wrestling, a men-only sport, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">January 30,</span> 2007</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AColorado&amp;rft.btitle=Colorado+Counties&amp;rft.date=2007-01-08&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=State+of+Colorado%2C+Department+of+Local+Affairs&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dola.state.co.us%2Fdlg%2Flocal_governments%2Fcounties.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-CSA-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CSA_110-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a> defines a <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">combined statistical area</a> (CSA) as an aggregate of adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">Core Based Statistical Areas</a> that are linked by commuting ties.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-MSA-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MSA_111-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a> defines a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> (MSA) as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">Core Based Statistical Area</a> having at least one urbanized area of 50,000 or more population, plus adjacent territory that has a high degree of social and economic integration with the core as measured by commuting ties.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-.CE.BCSA-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-.CE.BCSA_112-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a> defines a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Micropolitan Statistical Area">Micropolitan Statistical Area</a> (μSA) as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">Core Based Statistical Area</a> having at least one urban cluster of at least 10,000 but less than 50,000 population, plus adjacent territory that has a high degree of social and economic integration with the core as measured by commuting ties.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-OMB_10-02-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-OMB_10-02_113-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://obamawhitehouse.archives.gov/sites/default/files/omb/assets/bulletins/b10-02.pdf" rel="nofollow">"OMB Bulletin No. 10-02: Update of Statistical Area Definitions and Guidance on Their Uses"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a>. December 1, 2009<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">January 7,</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AColorado&amp;rft.btitle=OMB+Bulletin+No.+10-02%3A+Update+of+Statistical+Area+Definitions+and+Guidance+on+Their+Uses&amp;rft.date=2009-12-01&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=United+States+Office+of+Management+and+Budget&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fobamawhitehouse.archives.gov%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fomb%2Fassets%2Fbulletins%2Fb10-02.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul>
<li><cite><i>Explore Colorado, A Naturalist's Handbook</i></cite>, The Denver Museum of Natural History and Westcliff Publishers, 1995, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-56579-124-X" title="Special:BookSources/1-56579-124-X">1-56579-124-X</a> for an excellent guide to the ecological regions of Colorado.</li>
<li><cite><i>The Archeology of Colorado</i>, Revised Edition</cite>, E. Steve Cassells, Johnson Books, Boulder, Colorado, 1997, trade paperback, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-55566-193-9" title="Special:BookSources/1-55566-193-9">1-55566-193-9</a>.</li>
<li><cite><i>Chokecherry Places, Essays from the High Plains</i></cite>, Merrill Gilfillan, Johnson Press, Boulder, Colorado, trade paperback, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-55566-227-7" title="Special:BookSources/1-55566-227-7">1-55566-227-7</a>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/John_Gunther" title="John Gunther">Gunther, John</a> (1947). "–But Scenery Is Not Enough". <i><a href="/wiki/Inside_U.S.A._(book)" title="Inside U.S.A. (book)">Inside U.S.A.</a></i> <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harper_%26_Brothers" title="Harper &amp; Brothers">Harper &amp; Brothers</a>. pp. 213–226.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AColorado&amp;rft.atitle=%E2%80%93But+Scenery+Is+Not+Enough&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.aulast=Gunther&amp;rft.btitle=Inside+U.S.A.&amp;rft.date=1947&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.pages=213-226&amp;rft.place=New+York%2C+London&amp;rft.pub=Harper+%26+Brothers&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
<li><cite><i><a href="/wiki/The_Tie_That_Binds_(novel)" title="The Tie That Binds (novel)">The Tie That Binds</a></i></cite>, <a href="/wiki/Kent_Haruf" title="Kent Haruf">Kent Haruf</a>, 1984, hardcover, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-03-071979-8" title="Special:BookSources/0-03-071979-8">0-03-071979-8</a>, a fictional account of farming in Colorado.</li>
<li><cite><i>Railroads of Colorado: Your Guide to Colorado's Historic Trains and Railway Sites</i></cite>, Claude Wiatrowski, Voyageur Press, 2002, hardcover, 160 pages, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-89658-591-3" title="Special:BookSources/0-89658-591-3">0-89658-591-3</a></li>
<li><cite><i>Study Finds Legal Marijuana Motivates Many Tourists to Visit Colorado</i></cite>, (n.d.). Retrieved from <a class="external free" href="http://www.denverpost.com/business/ci_29225304/marijuana-has-huge-influence-colorado-tourism-state-survey" rel="nofollow">http://www.denverpost.com/business/ci_29225304/marijuana-has-huge-influence-colorado-tourism-state-survey</a></li>
